                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>

                  <foreign lang="ar">الوِلَادَةُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The act of bringing forth was rendered easy to her.</hi> (A.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">He made his circumstances ample; he made his condition,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">his way</hi> or <hi rend="ital">course</hi> [<foreign lang="ar">لِكَذَا</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">لِلْيُسْرَى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">to easy things,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">affairs,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">circumstances;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to the easier,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">easiest, way</hi>]: (S. A, [in the latter of which this is given as a proper, not tropical, signification:]) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">he prepared,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">made ready, him</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it,</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لِكَذَا</foreign>

                  <form>

                  </form> The <hi rend="ital">game,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">play, with unfeathered and headless arrows;</hi> (M, K;) the <hi rend="ital">game of hazard which the Arabs play with such arrows;</hi> (S, Mgh, Msb;) <hi rend="ital">a game of the Arabs, played</hi> [<hi rend="ital">by ten men,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">with ten unfeathered and headless arrows:</hi> they first slaughtered a camel, [bought on credit, (see below, in this paragraph,)] and divided it into ten portions, or, as some say, [agreeably with what follows,] into twenty-eight: the first arrow was called <foreign lang="ar">الفَذُّ</foreign>, and had [one notch and] one portion of the slaughtered camel: the second, <foreign lang="ar">التَّوْءَمُ</foreign>, and had [two notches and] two portions: the third, <foreign lang="ar">الرَّقِيبُ</foreign>, and had [three notches and] three portions: the fourth, <foreign lang="ar">الحِلْسُ</foreign>, and had [four notches and] four portions: the fifth, <foreign lang="ar">النَّافِسُ</foreign>, and had [five notches and] five portions; or, as some say, this was the fourth: the sixth, <foreign lang="ar">المُسْبِلُ</foreign>, and had [six notches and] six portions: the seventh, <foreign lang="ar">المُعَلَّى</foreign>, which was the highest of them, having [seven notches and] seven portions: the eighth and ninth and tenth were called <foreign lang="ar">السَّفِيحُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">المَنِيحُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الوَغْدُ</foreign>; and these three had no portions: [the players to whom these three fell had to pay for the slaughtered camel: (see <foreign lang="ar">المُسْبِلُ</foreign>:) whence it appears, that if the camel was divided into ten portions, (see <foreign lang="ar">رَيْمٌ</foreign>,) the game must have continued after all these were won, until it was seen whose were the eighth and ninth and tenth arrows; and it seems to be the general opinion that this was the case:] the camel being slaughtered, they collected together the ten arrows, and put them into the <foreign lang="ar">رِبَابَة</foreign>, a thing resembling a quiver (<foreign lang="ar">كِنَانَة</foreign>), and turned them round about or shuffled them (<foreign lang="ar">أَجَالُوهَا</foreign>): [or they employed a person, whom they called <foreign lang="ar">حُرْضَة</foreign>, to do this:] then they put them into the hand of the judge (<foreign lang="ar">الحَكَم</foreign>), who took them forth one after another in the name of one after another of the party; [or they commissioned the <foreign lang="ar">حُرْضَه</foreign> to do so;] and each took of the portions of the slaughtered camel according to his arrow; but those to whose lots fell the arrows without portions were obliged to pay the price of the slaughtered camel: with the flesh of which they afterwards fed the poor; and him who would not engage with them in the game they reproached, and called a <foreign lang="ar">بَرَم</foreign>: (Sefeenet Er-Rághib, printed at Boolák; p. 637:) [see also <foreign lang="ar">رَقِيبٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">ضَرِيبٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عَشْرٌ</foreign>:] or <hi rend="ital">any game of hazard;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">play for stakes, or wagers:</hi> (K:) so that even the game of children with walnuts is included under this name by Mujáhid in his explanation of verse 216 of chap. ii. of the Kur.: (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">anything in which is risk, or hazard:</hi> (Kull, p. 321:) or the <hi rend="ital">game of tricktrack, backgammon,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tables;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">نَرْدٌ</foreign>: (Sgh, K:) and <hi rend="ital">chess</hi> was called by 'Alee the <foreign lang="ar">مَيْسِر</foreign> of the Persians, or foreigners: (TA:) or the <hi rend="ital">slaughtered camel for which they played:</hi> for when they desired to play, they bought on credit a camel for slaughter, and slaughtered it, and divided it into twentyeight portions, or ten portions; and when one [of the arrows] after another came forth [from the <foreign lang="ar">رِبَابَة</foreign>] in the name of one man after another, the gain of him for whom came forth those to which belonged portions appeared, and the fine of him for whom came forth [any of the arrows called] the <foreign lang="ar">غُفْل</foreign>: (K:) so called as though it were a place of division: and so used by the poet Lebeed, who speaks of a fat <foreign lang="ar">مَيْسِر</foreign>.
